  ---------------------------------------------------------------------
Apache Kafka:
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0V9SK6jmDPk
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gg-VwXSRnmg&list=PLkz1SCf5iB4enAR00Z46JwY9GGkaS2NON&index=1


P2P Communication : If one Message is sent to one Consumer
Destination type is : Queue.

Publish-Subscribe [Pub/Sub] Communication:
  if one Message is sent to multiple consumers. Destination type : Topic.

So in Pub/Sub communication cade will remain same what we saw in P2P commnication just one thing we need to change which is in properties file make as spring.jms.pub-sub-domain as true ,if ir is false then it is P2P communcaition rest the code remains same almost

or 

In **Spring JMS**, for Pub/Sub communication the code mostly remains the same as we use in P2P communication. The main change is in the properties file where we set `spring.jms.pub-sub-domain=true` to use **Topic (Pub/Sub)**, and if it is set to `false` then it works as **Queue (P2P)**. However, it is not completely the same in all cases — sometimes we may need small changes like using a topic destination, handling multiple subscribers, or configuring durable subscriptions. Overall, the structure remains similar, but configuration and behavior differ slightly.


Around **80–90% of the code remains same**, only **10–20% changes** when switching from **P2P (Queue)** to **Pub/Sub (Topic)** in **Spring JMS**.

---

### 🔹 What stays same (Major part)

* **JmsTemplate usage**
* **Producer code**
* **Listener structure**
* **Message format / payload**

---

### 🔹 What changes (Minor part)

* **Property config** → `spring.jms.pub-sub-domain=true`
* **Destination type** → Queue ➝ Topic
* **Subscriber behavior** → Multiple consumers receive same message
* **Durable subscription (optional)**

---

### 🔹 Final Interview Line

👉 **Only ~10–20% configuration and behavior changes, rest (~80–90%) code remains same**


*) In Producer and Consumer applications we need to set one Property
   spring.jms.pub-sub-domain as true(make true on both the side producers and consumer application). Default is false.

=> false means P2P communication, true means Pub/sub.
=> Just define multiple consumers and set spring.jms.pub-sub-domain=true.
=> Cloned Copies of Actual Message is sent to multiple consumers.
=> Make Sure, all destination names (Producer and Consumer apps)
   must be matching.

Q) What if we delete topic from MQ Broker?
A) A new topic with same name is created. But old data will be removed.
  It is not a recomanded approch.

Q) What if we stop one consumer and start from some time?
  In case of P2P and Pub/Sub?

A)
 P2P : There will be only one consumer. So , all Producer mesages single
  copy is persisted at MOM Destination. Once consumer is up
  then all Messages are delivered.

 Pub/Sub : Based on No.of Consumers, Cloned Copies are created and sent to
  consumer applications. [not persisted]
  Ex: 3 consumers are connected first.
      1 Message in(Message enqued) = 3 Message out(Message dequed).
      If One Consumer is stopped in middle
      1 Message in = 2 Message out

Input x Consumers = Output
 5    x 0         = 0   (data lost)
 2    x 2         = 4   (delivered)


Q) Does ActiveMQ supports LoadBalancing?
   What if MOM S/w ActiveMQ is down?

A) ActiveMQ comes with single instance (No LoadBalance)
   if it is down data lose may occure.

   So to overcome this we use KAFKA.

=====Execution order===================
1. Start ActiveMQ
2. Start Consumer Application#1 and #2
3. Start Producer application



---------------------------------------------Lecture-99------------------------------------------------



 ---------------------------------------------------------------------
https://kafka.apache.org/quickstart

           Apache Kafka

*) It is a Open Source API used to connect multiple applications to
   send data (Message Queue)

*) Multi-Broker concept : it contains multiple brokers (Cluster)
   to send data to multiple consumers.

   [ActiveMQ - Single broker].

*) Scaling/Load Balancing can be done in Cluster.
*) Protocol independent (uses app protocol).

*) Kafka supports Pub/Sub Model only. No P2P. To send data to one consumer
   use only Pub/Sub in Kafka.

*) Full Kafka S/w is called as EcoSystem. This system contains mainly
  3 parts. They are:

  1. Zoo Keeper : Controls entire system.
  2. Kafka Cluster : Group of Message Brokers(old version: min 3, new version: min 1). so here in kafka we can create n number of message brokers. In Active MQ we have only one message broker. 
  3. Topics : it is a Memory that stores data in partitions


*) Data is exchanged in Serilized format ( data can be in this format-> String/JSON/XML Data)(it is not java serialization its kafka internal serialization)
*) Producer and Consumer both are connected using TopicName(destination name), So no Ip address and port number name is given to each means consumer will not give its ip address and port number to producer and same vice  versa so both producer and consumer are connected by using Topic name in between them.
*) By using KafkaTemplate<K,V> producer app will send data to Kafka.
   K = TopicName and V = Data
   and @KafkaListener(K) is used to read data at consumer app.
                      ↓
              here K is TopicName so with the help of TopicName consumer will read the data which is send by producer    

Producer sends data to a Topic using KafkaTemplate, and Consumer reads data from the same Topic using @KafkaListener.


how this Topics looks like from inside : 

*) Topics is a memory that holds data in packets formats [data blocks].
   Those are identified using index numbers starts from zero [offset]
   
    Here producer will send data to topics and topics is a memory that holds the data instead of sending the large data, data is converted into data packets/partition. These data packets is having some number we call them offset number which starts from zero u can create as many as u want. So we send tht data from the producers and this is stored in data packets/partitions

*) MR : Messsage Replica creates cloned copies of actual data to send
   it to consumer.

   whatever data producers sends to topics and that data is stored in data packets format in partions that partition data is been cloned / copied by Message Replica . so here message replica create cloned copies of the actual data which is present in data packets in topics 
   and that copied data is send to consumer from message replica  

*) ZooKeeper controls Eco-System like, create/manage topic, 
   allocate a broker to consumer, increase cluster size..etc

==========================================================================
Download : https://kafka.apache.org/downloads
Link: Scala 2.12  - kafka_2.12-2.8.1.tgz (asc, sha512)

// in realtime project point 1 and 2 is done by command only

 Consumer > Producer > Kafka server > ZooKeeper(stop in this order)


----------------------------------Lecture-100---------------------------------------------

---------------------------------------------------------------------
*) Kafka is Open Source and MQ S/w
*) Implemented by Apache
*) Uses LoadBalancer for Cluster (Multiple Message Broker)
*) Uses our application protocol
*) Kafka Supports only Pub/Sub Model (Topics).
   Even if we want to send message to one consumer use Topic only.
*) Kafka accepts only Serialized data for partitions.
*) Partitions contains index number [offset]

*) KafkaTemplate<K,V> is used at Producer application to send data
   to Kafka S/w

*) In case of non-Spring Boot application(Java app)
Ref this:
https://docs.spring.io/spring-kafka/reference/html/#with-java-configuration-no-spring-boot

*) Spring boot supports integration with kafka, we need to use JARs

<dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.kafka</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-kafka</artifactId>
</dependency>

*) It gives auto-configuration for KafkaTemplate<K,V> and @KafkaListener
*) Both Producer and Consumer are connected using TopicName.

    @Bean
    public NewTopic topic() {
        return TopicBuilder.name("myabc")
                .partitions(10)
                .replicas(1)
                .build();
    }   

or

@Bean
public NewTopic topic() {
    return TopicBuilder.name("myabc") // topic name is myabc
        .partitions(10) // topic will have 10 partitions (data is distributed across them)
        .replicas(1) // replication factor = 1 (only 1 copy, no backup)
        .build();
}


--cmd--
.\bin\windows\kafka-topics.bat 
  --create 
  --topic myabc 
  --partitions 10 
  --replicas 1
  --bootstrap-server localhost:9092

Q : how data is being stored in these partions?
Ans :
### 🔹 Simple Example (How data is stored in partitions in Apache Kafka)

👉 Suppose you have:

* **Topic = orders**
* **Partitions = 3 (P0, P1, P2)**

---

### 🔹 Producer sends messages

```
Order1, Order2, Order3, Order4, Order5
```

---

### 🔹 How Kafka stores them

👉 Kafka distributes messages like this:
this is round robin because here u dont have any key 

```
P0 → Order1, Order4  
P1 → Order2, Order5  
P2 → Order3
```

---

### 🔹 Simple Understanding

* Data is **not stored in one place**
* It is **spread across partitions**
* Each partition keeps **ordered data**

---

### 🔹 Important Point

* If **key is same** → goes to **same partition**
* If no key → Kafka distributes **round-robin**

---

### 🔹 Final One-liner

👉 **Kafka splits data across partitions so multiple consumers can read in parallel and improve performance**



and if keys are same : 

### 🔹 Example (Same Key → Same Partition) in Apache Kafka

👉 Suppose:

* **Partitions = P0, P1, P2**
* Key = **UserId**

---

### 🔹 Producer sends messages

```text
here if keys are same so here u see User1 is coming 3 time so we will put user1 data in partion-0 like this it works 
(Key  , Value )
(User1, Order1)
(User2, Order2)
(User1, Order3)
(User2, Order4)
(User1, Order5)
```

---

### 🔹 How Kafka stores them

```text
P0 → (User1, Order1), (User1, Order3), (User1, Order5)

P1 → (User2, Order2), (User2, Order4)

P2 → (empty or other users)
```

---

### 🔹 Simple Understanding

* Same key (**User1**) → always goes to **same partition (P0)**
* Same key (**User2**) → always goes to **same partition (P1)**

👉 This keeps **order maintained per key**

---

### 🔹 Why this is useful

* All data of one user stays **in order**
* Important for **banking, orders, transactions**

---

### 🔹 Final One-liner

👉 **Kafka uses key-based hashing, so same key always goes to same partition to maintain order**


//meaning of this Line replication factor = 1 (only 1 copy, no backup) below the answer is 


### 🔹 Simple Meaning (Replication Factor = 1) in Apache Kafka

👉 **Replication = how many copies of your data exist**

---

### 🔹 Example

* **replicas = 1**

  * 👉 Only **1 copy of data**
  * ❌ No backup

```text
Broker1 → Order1, Order2, Order3
```

---

### 🔹 If broker fails ❌

* Data is **lost**
* No other copy available

---

### 🔹 If replicas = 3 (for understanding)

```text
Broker1 → Order1
Broker2 → Order1 (copy)
Broker3 → Order1 (copy)
```

👉 Now even if one fails → data is safe ✅

---

### 🔹 Final One-liner

👉 **Replication factor = 1 means only one copy of data is stored, so there is no backup and risk of data loss** 

So, Replication factor = 1 means only one copy of data is stored, so there is no backup and risk of data loss.
So we keep higher replication (like 2 or 3) to maintain backup copies, so if one broker fails, data is still available.

   one copy of actual message)

  4 Consumers --> 1 Group --> Message Broker --> MR(4 copies)
  @KafkaListener takes topicName and groupId to read data from EcoSystem.

   and view output.

2. Entity
package com.app.raghu.entity;

import javax.persistence.Column;
import javax.persistence.Entity;
import javax.persistence.GeneratedValue;
import javax.persistence.GenerationType;
import javax.persistence.Id;
import javax.persistence.Table;

import lombok.Data;

@Data
@Entity
@Table(name="stocktab")
public class StockInfo {
  
  @Id
  @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
  @Column(name="sid")
  private Integer stkId;
  
  @Column(name="scode")
  private String stkCode;
  
  @Column(name="scost")
  private Double stkCost;
  
}

3. Repository
package com.app.raghu.repo;

import org.springframework.data.jpa.repository.JpaRepository;

import com.app.raghu.entity.StockInfo;

public interface StockInfoRepository extends JpaRepository<StockInfo, Integer> {

}

4. JSONUTIL
package com.app.raghu.util;

import com.app.raghu.entity.StockInfo;
import com.fasterxml.jackson.core.JsonProcessingException;
import com.fasterxml.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;

public class JsonUtil {

  public static StockInfo convertToObj(String message) {
    try {
      return new ObjectMapper().readValue(message, StockInfo.class);
    } catch (JsonProcessingException e) {
      e.printStackTrace();
    }
    return null;
  }

  public static String convertToString(StockInfo si) {
    try {
      return new ObjectMapper().writeValueAsString(si);
    } catch (JsonProcessingException e) {
      e.printStackTrace();
    }
    return null;
  }

}

5. MessageStore
package com.app.raghu.db;

import java.util.List;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

import com.app.raghu.entity.StockInfo;
import com.app.raghu.repo.StockInfoRepository;
import com.app.raghu.util.JsonUtil;

@Component
public class MessageStore {
  
  @Autowired
  private StockInfoRepository repo;

  public void add(String message) {
    //JSON TO Object
    StockInfo si = JsonUtil.convertToObj(message);
    repo.save(si);
  }

  public List<StockInfo> getAll() {
    return repo.findAll();
  }

}

6. Consumer Service
package com.app.raghu.service;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.kafka.annotation.KafkaListener;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

import com.app.raghu.db.MessageStore;

import lombok.extern.slf4j.Slf4j;

@Component
@Slf4j
public class ConsumerService {
  
  @Autowired
  private MessageStore store;

  @KafkaListener(topics = "${my.topic.name}",groupId = "abcd")
  public void readMessage(String message) {
    log.info("MESSAGE AT CONSUMER : {}", message);
    store.add(message);
  }
}


7. Producer service
package com.app.raghu.service;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Value;
import org.springframework.kafka.core.KafkaTemplate;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Component;

import lombok.extern.slf4j.Slf4j;

@Component
@Slf4j
public class ProducerService {

  @Autowired
  private KafkaTemplate<String, String> template;
  
  @Value("${my.topic.name}")
  private String topicName;
  
  public void sendMessage(String message) {
    log.info("MESSAGE IS AT PRODUCER SERVICE");
    template.send(topicName, message);
  }
}


8. RestController
package com.app.raghu.rest;

import java.util.List;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestParam;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

import com.app.raghu.db.MessageStore;
import com.app.raghu.entity.StockInfo;
import com.app.raghu.service.ProducerService;
import com.app.raghu.util.JsonUtil;

@RestController
@RequestMapping("/api/v1/kafka")
public class StockRestController {
  
  @Autowired
  private ProducerService service;
  
  @Autowired
  private MessageStore store;

  //send?code=__&cost=__
  @GetMapping("/send")
  public String readMessage(
      @RequestParam String code,
      @RequestParam Double cost
      ) 
  {
    //create Entity class object
    StockInfo si = new StockInfo();
    si.setStkCode(code);
    si.setStkCost(cost);
    
    //convert to JSON
    String message = JsonUtil.convertToString(si);
    
    //call producer service
    service.sendMessage(message);
    
    return "SENT";
  }
  
  @GetMapping("/all")
  public List<StockInfo> fetchAll() {
    return store.getAll();
  }
  
  
}

according to the above code the flow and statement is like this :
🔹 ONE LINE FLOW

👉 API → Producer → Kafka → Consumer → repo.save() → Database

   so after consumer receives message then it saves the data to database. So consumer connects to DB. 

Q : In real time also database is always connected to consumer not to producer? 
Ans: 
⚠️ **Not always — depends on use case**

---

### 🔹 Correct Understanding (Real-world)

👉 **Most common pattern (like your example)**

* Producer → sends event
* Consumer → saves to DB ✅

✔ Used in:

* Event-driven systems
* Microservices
* Kafka pipelines

---

### 🔹 But sometimes Producer also uses DB ❗

👉 Example:

* User places order
* Producer service:

  * ✅ Saves order in DB
  * ✅ Then sends event to Kafka

---

### 🔹 So final clarity

* **Consumer → usually writes to DB (very common)**
* **Producer → may or may not use DB (depends on design)**

---

### 🔹 Final Interview Line ⭐

👉 **In most Kafka-based systems, consumers handle data persistence, but producers can also interact with databases depending on the use case**

package com.app.raghu;

import com.app.raghu.entity.StockInfo;
import com.fasterxml.jackson.databind.ObjectMapper;

public class Test {
  
  //JSON to Object
  public static void main(String[] args) {
    String json ="{\"stkId\":101,\"stkCode\":\"A\",\"stkCost\":200.0}";
    
    try {
      ObjectMapper om = new ObjectMapper();
      StockInfo si = om.readValue(json, StockInfo.class);
      System.out.println(si);
    } catch (Exception e) {
      e.printStackTrace();
    }
  }

  //Object to JSON
  public static void main1(String[] args) {
    StockInfo si = new StockInfo();
    si.setStkCode("A");
    si.setStkCost(200.0);
    si.setStkId(101);
    
    try {
      ObjectMapper om = new ObjectMapper();
      String s = om.writeValueAsString(si);
      System.out.println(s);
    } catch (Exception e) {
      e.printStackTrace();
    }
  }
}

Topic: Apache Kafka supports only Topics to send data even for 1 to 1 also.
 No P2P -- Queue concept in kafka. Everything is Pub/Sub -- Topic 

@Bean
public NewTopic topic() {
       return TopicBuilder.name("topic1")
               .partitions(10) //based on message sizes
               .replicas(1) // no.of consumers
               .build();
}
//default values are : partitions=1 , replicas =1 
(or) KafkaTemplate creates given topic name on the fly (at runtime)

*)Group : Logical unit of a multiple consumers which are using same topicName
 In this case MessageBroker informs MessageReplica to create Cloned Copies

 ex: group=abc, consumers=5 , topicName=TEST-A
  MessageBroker-5 is allocated, MR-5 copies of actual message from TEST-A

======================================================================
*) When ever KafkaTemplate calls send method then Kafka API creates one object
  ProducerRecord (C)

Internal code: Data --> Serialized
ProducerRecord<K, V> producerRecord = new ProducerRecord<>(topic, data);

*) @KafkListener that reads data from given topicName into ConsumerRecord(C)

//Data -> Deserialized
ConsumerRecord<K,V> consumerRecord = new ConsumerRecord<>(topic,data);

*) Internally data format is binary (byte[]) easy for trasfer and partitions

=> One consumer can read data from multiple topics too.
Ex:
@KafkaListener(topics = {
           "${my.topic.name2}",
     "${my.topic.name1}",
     "${my.topic.name3}"
         },
  groupId = "abcd")


*) Spring with Kafka uses MessagingMessageListenerAdapter(C)
 which is a Listener class that reads data from Kafka broker and
 converts data. 

*) Our application is connected with Kafka Server that runs on port : 9092
  Zookeeper runs on port: 2181

Q : What is fault tolerance ? 
Ans : 
## 🔹 **Fault Tolerance (Simple Meaning)**

👉 **Fault tolerance means a system keeps working even if something fails**

---

## 🔹 **Easy Example**

* Suppose 1 server crashes ❌
* Another server takes over ✔️

👉 User doesn’t face any problem → this is **fault tolerance**

---

## 🔹 **Real-Life Example**

* In banking apps 💳
* Even if one system fails, transaction still works

---

## 🔹 **In Simple Words**

👉 **“System should not stop even if parts fail”**

---

## 🔹 **Key Idea**

* Failure will happen ❗
* System should **handle it smoothly**

---

## 🔹 **One Line Answer (Interview)**

👉 **Fault tolerance is the ability of a system to continue working even when some components fail**


Q : how can we achieve fault tolerence in kafka ? 
Ans : 
## 🔹 **Fault Tolerance in Apache Kafka (Simple)**

👉 Kafka stays working even if a server fails by using **replication + distributed setup**

---

## 🔹 **How Kafka achieves it**

1. **Replication (Most Important)**

   * Each topic data is copied to **multiple brokers**
   * One is **leader**, others are **followers**

2. **Leader–Follower Mechanism**

   * Producer/consumer talks to **leader**
   * If leader fails ❌ → follower becomes **new leader ✔️**

3. **Multiple Brokers (Cluster)**

   * Kafka runs on many servers
   * If one server goes down → others still work

4. **Acknowledgement (acks)**

   * `acks=all` → data is safe in **multiple replicas**
   * Prevents data loss

5. **ISR (In-Sync Replicas)**

   * Only synced replicas can become leader
   * Ensures **data consistency**

---

## 🔹 **Simple Flow**

👉 Producer → Leader → Followers (copy data)
👉 Leader fails → Follower becomes leader → system continues

---

## 🔹 **One Line Answer (Interview)**

👉 Kafka achieves fault tolerance using **replication, multiple brokers, and automatic leader switching**

Q : How can we achieve durability in Kafka ? 
Ans : ## 🔹 **Durability in Apache Kafka (Simple)**

👉 **Durability means data is NOT lost even after crashes or restart**

---

## 🔹 **How Kafka achieves durability**

1. **Replication**

   * Data is stored in **multiple brokers**
   * If one fails → other copies are safe

2. **Write to Disk (Persistent Storage)**

   * Kafka writes messages to **disk (not only memory)**
   * So data stays even after restart

3. **Acknowledgement (`acks=all`)**

   * Producer waits until **all replicas store data**
   * Ensures strong durability

4. **In-Sync Replicas (ISR)**

   * Only **fully synced replicas** are used
   * Prevents data inconsistency

5. **Log Retention**

   * Messages are stored for **configured time/size**
   * Not deleted immediately

---

## 🔹 **Simple Flow**

👉 Producer sends data → stored on disk + replicated
👉 Even if broker crashes → data still available ✔️

---

## 🔹 **One Line Answer (Interview)**

👉 Kafka achieves durability using **replication, disk storage, and acknowledgements (acks=all)**

Q : how can we achieve parelalism in kafka ?
Ans : 

## 🔹 **Parallelism in Apache Kafka (Simple)**

👉 **Parallelism means processing multiple messages at the same time**

---

## 🔹 **How Kafka achieves it**

1. **Partitions (Main concept)**

   * Topic is divided into **multiple partitions**
   * Each partition can be processed **independently**

2. **Multiple Consumers**

   * Same consumer group → each consumer reads **different partition**
   * So work happens **in parallel**

3. **Consumer Group**

   * Kafka distributes partitions among consumers
   * Example:

     * 3 partitions → 3 consumers → all work together

4. **Multiple Brokers**

   * Partitions are spread across servers
   * Improves parallel processing

---

## 🔹 **Simple Example**

👉 Topic has 3 partitions
👉 3 consumers in same group

* Consumer 1 → Partition 1
* Consumer 2 → Partition 2
* Consumer 3 → Partition 3

👉 All process data **at same time ✔️**

---

## 🔹 **One Line Answer (Interview)**

👉 Kafka achieves parallelism using **partitions and multiple consumers in a consumer group**


Q : suppose we have 50 producers and 50 consumers and still some of the consumer s are running slow what could be the reason and yes assume that kafka ecosystem , kafka cluster, broker is fit and fine ?

Ans :
## 🔹 **Full Answer (Interview Ready – Simple & Clear)**

👉 Even if **Kafka cluster is perfectly fine**, some consumers can still be slow due to **data distribution and processing issues**

---

## 🔹 **1. Uneven Data Distribution (Main Reason)**

* Kafka divides data into **partitions**
* Each consumer reads **one partition**

👉 If data is **not evenly distributed**:

* One partition = **heavy (more messages)**
* Other partitions = **light**

👉 Result:

* Consumer handling heavy partition → **slow**
* Others → **fast**

---

## 🔹 **2. Why uneven distribution happens**

### ✔️ **When key is present**

* Same key → goes to **same partition**
* If one key is used a lot → **hot partition 🔥**

---

### ✔️ **When key = null**

* Kafka uses **round-robin / sticky partitioning**
* Data is **almost evenly distributed**

👉 But:

* Not **100% perfect balance**
* Still slight difference can happen

---

## 🔹 **3. Other reasons (Very Important)**

1. **Slow Consumer Logic**

   * DB calls, API calls, heavy processing

2. **Blocking / Single Thread**

   * Consumer processes one message at a time

3. **Large Messages**

   * Bigger data → more processing time

4. **Rebalancing**

   * Consumers joining/leaving → temporary slowdown

---

## 🔹 **4. Simple Example**

* Partition 1 → 10,000 messages
* Partition 2 → 2,000 messages

👉 Consumer 1 = slow
👉 Consumer 2 = fast

---

## 🔹 **Final Answer (Best for Interview)**

👉 Even with a healthy Kafka cluster, consumers can be slow due to **uneven partition distribution (hot partitions), slow processing logic, blocking code, or large messages**

---

## 🔹 **One Line Summary**

👉 **Uneven data + slow processing = slow consumers**




Here is your **notes explained in short & simple terms (interview style)** 👇

---

# 🔹 **1. Overall Flow**

👉 **Producer → Kafka Cluster (Brokers) → Consumer**

* Producer sends data
* Kafka stores it
* Consumer reads it

---

# 🔹 **2. ACK (Acknowledgement)**

👉 It tells **how safely data is stored**

1. **acks = 0**

   * No confirmation
   * Fastest ⚡
   * Risk: **data loss**

2. **acks = 1**

   * Only **leader stores data**
   * Medium safety

3. **acks = all**

   * Leader + followers store data
   * Safest ✔️
   * Slowest

👉 **Best for durability = acks=all**

---

# 🔹 **3. Topic, Partition, Replication**

👉 Example:

* Topic = **Order**
* Partitions = **5**
* Replication = **3**

👉 Meaning:

* Each partition has **3 copies (replicas)**
* Stored on different brokers

---

# 🔹 **4. Leader & Followers (Zookeeper role)**

👉 Apache ZooKeeper manages:

* Which replica is **Leader**
* Which are **Followers**

👉 Example:

* Leader → handles read/write
* Followers → copy data

👉 If leader fails ❌
👉 Zookeeper makes follower → **new leader ✔️**
    So here Zookeper decide whom to make leader 

---

# 🔹 **5. Rack Awareness**

👉 Kafka spreads replicas across **different machines/racks**

👉 So if one rack fails:

* Data still safe ✔️

---

# 🔹 **6. Delivery Modes (DEL Mode)**

👉 Defines **message guarantee**

1. **At-least-once**

   * No data loss ✔️
   * But **duplicates possible**

2. **At-most-once**

   * No duplicates ✔️
   * But **data loss possible**

3. **Exactly-once**

   * No loss ✔️
   * No duplicate ✔️
   * Best but complex

---

# 🔹 **7. Consumer Commit Logic**

👉 After processing:

* Consumer commits offset

👉 If commit fails:

* Message may be **reprocessed (duplicate)**

---

# 🔹 **Final Interview Answer**

👉 Kafka ensures:

* **Durability** → replication + acks=all
* **Fault tolerance** → leader-follower + Zookeeper
* **Delivery guarantee** → at-least / at-most / exactly once

---

# 🔹 **One Line Summary**

👉 Kafka = **safe storage + replication + smart message delivery system** 🚀

## 🔹 **Q1: How to handle exceptions in Kafka?**

👉 **Short Answer (Interview)**

1. **Try-Catch in Consumer**

   * Wrap processing logic
   * Prevent consumer from crashing

2. **Retry Mechanism**

   * Retry failed message **2–3 times**

3. **Dead Letter Topic (DLT)**

   * If still fails → send message to **DLT**
   * So main flow doesn’t stop

   or 

   Dead Letter Queue (DLQ)
   If still fails → send message to DLQ
   So main flow doesn’t stop
   
   “DLQ and DLT are the same concept. If a message fails after retries, it will go to DLT in Kafka (or DLQ in other systems(Rabbit MQ , Active MQ)).”

   and kafka works on topic so specifically we use DLT 


4. **Logging & Monitoring**

   * Log error for debugging

5. **Idempotent Processing**

   * Handle duplicates safely

---

👉 **One Line Answer**
👉 Handle exceptions using **try-catch, retry, and Dead Letter Topic (DLT)**

---

## 🔹 **Q2: Where did you use Kafka in your PinSafe (Card Vault) project?**

👉 **Project-Based Answer (Simple & Strong)**

1. **Asynchronous Processing**

   * Used Kafka to **decouple services**

2. **Payment Flow**

   * When card transaction comes →
     👉 Producer sends event to Kafka

3. **Encryption Service**

   * Consumer reads message →
     👉 Encrypts card data (HSM integration)

4. **Notification / Audit**

   * Another consumer logs transaction or sends alerts

5. **High Throughput**

   * Kafka handles **large number of transactions**

---

👉 **Simple Flow**

👉 API → Producer → Kafka → Consumer → Encryption / DB / Notification

👉 **One Line Answer (Interview)**
👉 We used Kafka for **asynchronous communication between services like payment, encryption, and audit logging in Card Vault system**

Here are all **15 Kafka interview questions with short, simple paragraph answers (ready to speak in interview)** 👇
(based on your PDF )

---

## 🔹 **1. What is ISR in Kafka? Why is it important?**

👉 ISR (In-Sync Replicas) are the replicas that are fully synced with the leader. Kafka only acknowledges data when it is written to all ISR replicas, which ensures **data durability and prevents data loss**.

---

## 🔹 **2. How does Kafka handle message ordering?**

👉 Kafka guarantees ordering **within a partition only**. If we use the same key, messages go to the same partition and maintain order. Partition count and key selection impact ordering.

---

## 🔹 **3. How does Kafka achieve high throughput and low latency?**

👉 Kafka uses **sequential disk writes, batching, and zero-copy mechanism**, which reduces overhead and makes data processing very fast.

---

## 🔹 **4. What is Exactly Once Semantics (EOS)?**

👉 EOS ensures that messages are processed **only once, without duplicates or data loss**. It is achieved using **idempotent producers and transactions**.

---

## 🔹 **5. What is the role of __consumer_offsets topic?**

👉 It stores the **offsets of consumers**, so Kafka knows which messages are already consumed. This helps in **fault tolerance and recovery**.

---

## 🔹 **6. How do partitions affect scalability?**

👉 Partitions allow **parallel processing**, so more partitions increase scalability. But too many partitions can cause **memory and management overhead**.

---

## 🔹 **7. What happens when a Kafka broker goes down?**

👉 If a broker fails, Kafka automatically selects a **new leader from ISR replicas**, so data remains available and system continues working.

---

## 🔹 **8. Difference between acks=0, acks=1, acks=all?**

👉

* **acks=0** → no confirmation, fast but risk of data loss
* **acks=1** → leader confirms, medium safety
* **acks=all** → all replicas confirm, slow but safest

---

## 🔹 **9. What is the role of Zookeeper in Kafka?**

👉 Zookeeper manages **cluster metadata, broker coordination, and leader election**, ensuring smooth cluster operation.

---

## 🔹 **10. Kafka Connect vs Kafka Streams?**

👉 Kafka Connect is used for **data integration (ETL)**, while Kafka Streams is used for **real-time data processing inside applications**.

---

## 🔹 **11. How to handle schema evolution in Kafka?**

👉 Use **Avro/Protobuf with Schema Registry**. Follow rules like **adding optional fields and not removing required fields** to maintain compatibility.

---

## 🔹 **12. How to monitor and tune Kafka performance?**

👉 Use tools like **JMX, Prometheus, Grafana** to monitor lag, throughput, etc. Tune configs like **batch size, linger.ms, fetch size**.

---

## 🔹 **13. What are drawbacks of high number of partitions?**

👉 More partitions improve parallelism but increase **metadata overhead, leader election time, and load on brokers/Zookeeper**.

---

## 🔹 **14. What is rebalancing in Kafka?**

👉 Rebalancing happens when consumers join/leave. Kafka redistributes partitions among consumers. It can be optimized using **cooperative rebalancing**.

---

## 🔹 **15. How to avoid data loss and duplication in Kafka?**

👉 Use **idempotent producers, transactions, acks=all, and proper offset management** to ensure safe and reliable processing.

---

## 🔹 **Final Tip**

👉 Speak like this:

* Keep it **simple**
* Use **keywords (ISR, partition, acks, etc.)**
* Don’t over-explain

---

one page kafka cheat sheet 

Here is your **🔥 Kafka 1-Page Cheat Sheet (Super Simple)** — revise this before interview 👇

---

# 🚀 **KAFKA CHEAT SHEET (Simple & Clear)**

## 🔹 **1. What is Kafka?**

👉 Kafka is a **message broker (middleman)**
👉 Used to send data between services

👉 **Flow:**
➡️ API → Producer → Kafka → Consumer → DB

---

## 🔹 **2. Core Components**

* **Producer** → sends data
* **Consumer** → reads data
* **Broker** → server (Kafka machine)
* **Topic** → like folder (stores messages)
* **Partition** → split of topic
* **Offset** → message ID

---

## 🔹 **3. Partition Concept**

👉 Topic is divided into partitions

* Helps in **parallel processing**
* Each partition has **ordered data**

👉 Rule:

* Same key → same partition ✔️
* No key → round-robin ✔️

---

## 🔹 **4. Consumer Group**

👉 Multiple consumers share work

* 1 partition → 1 consumer
* More partitions → more parallelism

---

## 🔹 **5. Replication (Safety)**

👉 Data is copied to multiple brokers

* **Leader** → main
* **Followers** → backup

👉 If leader fails → follower becomes leader

---

## 🔹 **6. ACK (Data Safety)**

* **acks=0** → fast, unsafe
* **acks=1** → medium
* **acks=all** → safest ✔️

---

## 🔹 **7. Delivery Guarantee**

* **At-least-once** → duplicate possible
* **At-most-once** → data loss possible
* **Exactly-once** → best (no loss, no duplicate)

---

## 🔹 **8. Offset (Very Important)**

👉 Consumer tracks offset

* If crash → resume from last offset

---

## 🔹 **9. Fault Tolerance**

👉 System works even if broker fails

👉 Done using:

* Replication
* Leader switching

---

## 🔹 **10. Durability**

👉 Data is safe even after restart

👉 Because:

* Stored on disk
* Replicated

---

## 🔹 **11. Parallelism**

👉 Achieved using:

* Partitions
* Consumer groups

---

## 🔹 **12. Common Problems**

👉 Slow consumer:

* Uneven data (hot partition)
* Heavy processing

👉 Data loss:

* low replication
* acks not set properly

---

## 🔹 **13. Error Handling**

👉 Use:

* Try-Catch
* Retry
* **DLT (Dead Letter Topic)**

---

## 🔹 **14. One Line Definitions**

* **Kafka** → message broker
* **Topic** → data container
* **Partition** → split of topic
* **Offset** → message position
* **Consumer Group** → parallel consumers

---

# 🔹 **FINAL INTERVIEW LINE**

👉 **Kafka is a distributed messaging system that provides high throughput, fault tolerance, and scalability using topics, partitions, and replication**

---

# 🔹 **ULTIMATE SIMPLIFICATION**

👉 Kafka = **WhatsApp for systems 📩**

* Producer → sender
* Kafka → server
* Consumer → receiver

---

--------------------------------Lecture-103---------------------------------------


---------------------------------------------------------------------
         Spring Cloud : API Gateway


API Gateway : It is a single entry and exit point for our MS# application.

=> There may be multiple MS# apps running as multiple Instances
=> All these microserives details are stored at Eureka Server
=> Eureka Server is a Register (Store data). 
     It never makes any HTTP call to any MS#
=> We can not expose all MS# IP and PORTs to client machine/app.
   We should give only one IP and PORT ie Gateway IP and PORT.

Why Gateway?
1. Routing : Dispatching a client request to MS# application
2. LoadBalancing : Choose one Instance from Eureka based on LoadFactor
      for every request
3. Filters : Modify Request/ Response details (Encryption, Authentication..etc)

Dynamic Routing | Dynamic Dispatching : Routing + Load Balancing.

*) Router needs Input as Routing table which is configured by Developers
*) Predicate compares Request Path with Routertable path if matching
   returns true means select MS# serviceId and goto eureka.

*) Pre-Filter(optional), if exist Modify the request before sending to MS# app.
   Post-Filter(optional), if exist Modify the Response before sending to Client.
   
*) Gateway also one type of MS#, It needs to be register with Eureka.
   It uses Porxy client (Feign) generated at Gateway, to make call to MS#.


Here is the **exact ordered text (points 1 → 11)** from your image:

---

### 🔹 Steps in Order how api gateway works

1 ⇒ **Request from Client**
2 ⇒ **Router reads Request**
3 ⇒ **Request goes to Routing table, compare URL with Path**

4 ⇒ **Get MS# ServiceId and go to Eureka to fetch MS# data where eureka will give us microservices id and also give that which instance is getting less load so route to that **
or
API Gateway gets the ServiceId and calls Eureka Server to fetch available service instances. Eureka returns all instances, and then the Gateway (using load balancer) selects one instance (usually least load / round-robin) and routes the request.

5 ⇒ **Returns ServiceInstance from Eureka**
6 ⇒ **Generates Proxy Client (Feign client)**
7 ⇒ **Pre-Filter is executed if exist (modify request)**
8 ⇒ **Execute RestController methods based on Path**
9 ⇒ **Return Response Entity and Post Filter is called**
10 ⇒ **Response is returned from Gateway**
11 ⇒ **Response given back to client**

---

==========================================================================
*) Spring Cloud API Gateway Routing(or Config) can be defined in two ways
1. YAML/Properties file
2. ***Java based Config(mostly used)
---EXAMPLE ROUTING TABLE ------------------
    PATH                    URI                          
  /order/**          lb://ORDER-SERVICE

  /cart/**           lb://CART-SERVICE
--------------------------------------------
If request URL contains /order in Path
//here localhost:80 is the port number of api gateway
ex: http://localhost:80/order/find/10 
  then select ORDER-SERVICE goto Eureka, fetch one ORDER-SERVICE instance
    and execute request for path "/order/find/10"

Api gateway using Java based Config
===Example Java Config=========================================
Dep : Gateway, Eureka Discovery Client

1. Config class for Routing table


package com.app.raghu.config;

import org.springframework.cloud.gateway.route.RouteLocator;
import org.springframework.cloud.gateway.route.builder.RouteLocatorBuilder;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;

@Configuration
public class MyRouteConfig {

  //use lb://ServiceId for multiple instance of MS#
  //use  this http://IP:PORT for single instance of MS# so no lb
  @Bean
  public RouteLocator configRoutes(RouteLocatorBuilder builder) {
    
    return builder.routes()
        //.route("cartRoutingId", r->r.path("/cart/**").uri("http://172.10.12.36:9696")) //one cart instance only
        .route("cartRoutingId", r->r.path("/cart/**").uri("lb://CART-SERVICE"))
        .route("orderRoutingId", r->r.path("/order/**").uri("lb://ORDER-SERVICE"))
        .build();
  }
}
.route("cartRoutingId", r->r.path("/cart/**").uri("lb://CART-SERVICE")//here lb is load balancer load balancer of cart service  


2. properties file
#server.port=80
server.port=9600

# Register with eureka
eureka.client.service-url.defaultZone=http://localhost:8761/eureka


---------------------------------Lecture-104-----------------------------------------

      Spring Cloud : API Gateway

1. Routing : Request --> MS# using Eureka
2. Loadbalancing : Choose one Instance has less LF (Round Robin)
3. Filters : Modify Request/Response

*) Router is a pre-defined component that taking Routing table data.
  Routing table must be configured by Programmer.

  Routing table = PATH + URI(serviceId/IP:PORT/HOSTNAME)

  ---------------------------------------------------------
     ID           PATH                     URI
  ---------------------------------------------------------
     CID        /cart/**              lb://CART-SERVICE
     OID  /order/**             lb://ORDER-SERVICE
  ---------------------------------------------------------

=> Every Routing table contains List<Route>
=>  1 route contains = 1 id + 1 path + 1 uri + multiple filters
    1 MS = 1 route

=> Eureka gives ServiceInstance(serviceId,InstanceId, IP, PORT, LF(load factor))

=> If a MS# which is not configured at ApiGateway can never be
   accessed from outside world.

Step#1 Define one Application for ApiGateway with 2 dependencies
a. Spring Cloud Gateway
b. Eureka Discovery Client

Step#2 Must be Registed with Eureka Server

--application.properties---
server.port=80
#server.port=9600

spring.application.name=API-GATEWAY

# Register with eureka
eureka.client.service-url.defaultZone=http://localhost:8761/eureka

Step#3 Define Java Configuration for Routing Table configuration
 RouteLocator stores List<Route> / Flux<Route>
 (Reactive Programming: Mono-1, Flux-n objects)

package com.app.raghu.config;

import org.springframework.cloud.gateway.route.RouteLocator;
import org.springframework.cloud.gateway.route.builder.RouteLocatorBuilder;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;

@Configuration
public class MyRouteConfig {

  @Bean
  public RouteLocator configureRoutes(RouteLocatorBuilder builder) {

    return builder.routes()
        .route("cartId", r -> r.path("/cart/**").uri("lb://CART-SERVICE"))
        .route("orderId", r -> r.path("/order/**").uri("lb://ORDER-SERVICE"))
        .build();
  }

}

==code changes====================================
1. API Gateway
package com.app.raghu.config;

import java.util.UUID;

import org.springframework.cloud.gateway.route.RouteLocator;
import org.springframework.cloud.gateway.route.builder.RouteLocatorBuilder;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;

@Configuration
public class MyRouteConfig {

  @Bean
  public RouteLocator configureRoutes(RouteLocatorBuilder builder) {

    return builder.routes()

        .route("cartId", r -> r.path("/cart/**")
            .filters(f->
            f.addRequestHeader("MyToken", "Basic "+UUID.randomUUID().toString())
            .addResponseHeader("Service-Mode", "Active")
            )
            
            .uri("lb://CART-SERVICE"))
        .route("orderId", r -> r.path("/order/**").uri("lb://ORDER-SERVICE")).build();
  }

}

  private String title;

  @GetMapping("/info")
  public ResponseEntity<String> showMessage(
      @RequestHeader("MyToken") String token 
      )
  {
    return ResponseEntity.ok("WELCOME TO CART SERVICE =>" + token);
  }
  ....
}

Equal YAML Configuration for API Gateway:

eureka:
  client:
    service-url:
      defaultZone: http://localhost:8761/eureka
server:
  port: 80
spring:
  application:
    name: API-GATEWAY
  cloud:
    gateway:
      routes:
      - id: cartId
        uri: lb://CART-SERVICE
        predicates:
        - Path=/cart/**
        filters:
        - AddRequestHeader=MyToken,BasicTEST
        - AddResponseHeader=Service-Mode, Active
      - id: orderId
        uri: lb://ORDER-SERVICE
        predicates:
        - Path=/order/**

         ->MS#2-->MS#1-> Gateway --> Resp#1

1. No of MS# called
2. Execution Path (method->Method)
3. Time taken for exact service and all services

=> It is type of debugging (Flow Debug).
=> Spring Cloud API has given : Sleuth and Zipkin to handle 
  "Distributed Tracing"

=> Sleuth : Generates details like Tracing Info/Execution Path/
            Execution Time. So slueth is like generating the details and giving to zipkin server and then zipkin server will show the details here details are like no of microservices, execution path and tracing many more....  

            in latest slueth is now replaced with micrometer tracing so what slueth was doing earlier now micrometer tracing is doing that

### 🔹 Micrometer Tracing Integration (Spring Boot – simple steps)

---

### 1️⃣ **Add Dependencies**

👉 For **Zipkin**

```xml
<dependency>
    <groupId>io.micrometer</groupId>
    <artifactId>micrometer-tracing-bridge-brave</artifactId>
</dependency>

<dependency>
    <groupId>io.zipkin.reporter2</groupId>
    <artifactId>zipkin-reporter-brave</artifactId>
</dependency>
```

👉 (Optional) Actuator

```xml
<dependency>
    <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
    <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-actuator</artifactId>
</dependency>
```

---

### 2️⃣ **Add Configuration (application.properties)**

```properties
management.tracing.sampling.probability=1.0
management.zipkin.tracing.endpoint=http://localhost:9411/api/v2/spans
```

👉 `1.0` = trace all requests

---

### 3️⃣ **Run Zipkin Server**

👉 Using Docker:

```bash
docker run -d -p 9411:9411 openzipkin/zipkin
```

---

### 4️⃣ **Run Your Spring Boot App**

* No extra code needed
* Tracing works **automatically**

---

### 5️⃣ **Verify**

👉 Open: `http://localhost:9411`
👉 You will see:

* **TraceId**
* **Request flow (microservices)**
* **Execution time**

---

### 🔹 What happens internally

* Micrometer generates **TraceId & SpanId**
* Tracks **request flow**
* Sends data to **Zipkin**
* Zipkin **stores & shows UI**

---

### 🔹 One Line

👉 **Add dependency + config → Micrometer automatically traces requests and sends data to Zipkin**

---

### 🔹 Interview Line

👉 **We integrate Micrometer Tracing by adding dependencies and configuration; it automatically generates trace data and sends it to Zipkin for monitoring distributed requests.**

package com.app.raghu.config;

import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.web.client.RestTemplate;

@Configuration
public class AppConfig {
  
  @Bean
  public RestTemplate rt() {
    return new RestTemplate();
  }

}

*)Define RestController
package com.app.raghu.rest;

import org.slf4j.Logger;
import org.slf4j.LoggerFactory;
import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;
import org.springframework.web.client.RestTemplate;

@RestController
public class ProcessARestController {
  
  private static final Logger log = LoggerFactory.getLogger(ProcessARestController.class);

  @Autowired
  private RestTemplate rt;
  
  @GetMapping("/showA")
  public String showMsg() {
    log.info("WE ARE AT A SERVICE...");
    
    String resp = rt.getForEntity("http://localhost:8082/showB", String.class).getBody();
    
    return "FROM A.."+resp;
  }
}

*) Repeate same for multiple MS# applications
  ServiceB, ServiceC examples.

*) Sleuth and Zipkin stores data using Logs and format looks like
 [ServiceName, TraceId, spanId, ExportFlag]

TraceId: Id generated for one entire request flow
spanId : Id generated for one MS# request flow.
parentId: Previous MS# spanId is current MS# parentId


TraceId = one for entire request flow (end-to-end tracking)
SpanId = unique for each microservice method call

TraceId and SpanId are automatically generated by Micrometer Tracing /Slueth without writing any manual code, ensuring end-to-end request tracking across microservices.

http://localhost:8081/showA

-----------------------------------------Lecture-108----------------------------------


---------------------------------------------------------------------
        Spring Boot Reactive Programming

*) Spring Boot WEB (MVC and REST)
starter: spring-boot-starter-web
@Controller, @RestController, @RequestMapping, @GetMapping...
@ModelAttribute, Model ..etc


*) Server: *Tomcat, Undertow, Jetty..etc
*) Tomcat is the default server, that allocates one Thread for one Request
 which will process request and returns response.

*) By default every Thread allocated to process is "BLOCKING MODEL".
 ie Thread if is making NIO(Network input output) call, then it will be idel, it will not process any other request meanwhile.(so the meaning of this line is that untinl the thread 1 fulfill the request of request 1 it will not go to request 2)

 or 

 By default, every thread works in a blocking model. This means when a thread makes a network I/O call (like calling another service or database), it becomes idle and waits for the response. During this waiting time, the thread cannot process any other request. In simple terms, a thread will complete one request fully before moving to the next request.

*) NON BLOCKING MODE says do not keep any thread idel.
   Use it for another request processing if is waiting for NIO call output.
   once we get NIO output allocate same thread or different one for
   processing response.

=> Spring Boot WebFlux (Spring 5.x), comes with Netty Server.
=> We need to use NoSQL DB like MongoDB, Redis..etc
    stores: JSON Format/Documents Data

Ouptput: Mono<T> (0/1), Flux<T> (0..n) output.


=> We have to use Spring boot reavtie API which is implemented using
   Spring Webflux. Here DB are used NoSQL Reactive suported.

Q : Can we use web client with spring boot rest(spring mvc) ? 
Ans: ### 🔹 Spring Boot REST + WebClient (simple)

👉 **Yes, you can use WebClient inside normal Spring Boot REST (Spring MVC)**

---

### 🔹 How it works

👉 Your app:

* Uses **@RestController (normal REST)**
* Uses **WebClient to call other APIs**

---

### 🔹 Example Code

```java
@RestController
public class MyController {

    private WebClient webClient = WebClient.create("http://user-service");

    @GetMapping("/getUser")
    public String getUser() {
        return webClient.get()
                .uri("/user/101")
                .retrieve()
                .bodyToMono(String.class)
                .block(); // blocking here
    }
}
```

---

### 🔹 Important Point

* `.block()` → makes it **blocking (like RestTemplate)**
* Without `.block()` → **reactive (non-blocking)**

---

### 🔹 When to use

👉 Use in Spring MVC when:

* You want **modern HTTP client** instead of RestTemplate

👉 Use in WebFlux when:

* You want **full non-blocking system**

---

### 🔹 One Line

👉 **WebClient can be used in normal Spring Boot REST, but becomes blocking if we use .block()**

---

### 🔹 Interview Line

👉 **In Spring Boot REST applications, WebClient can be used as an alternative to RestTemplate; however, if we call .block(), it behaves as a blocking call.**


Q : which is mostly used spring boot rest or spring web flux ? 
Ans : 

### 🔹 Short Answer

👉 **Spring REST (Spring MVC) is mostly used in real projects**

---

### 🔹 Why Spring REST is more used

1️⃣ **Simple & stable**

* Easy to understand and implement

2️⃣ **Huge ecosystem support**

* Works with all tools (JPA, MySQL, etc.)

3️⃣ **Most projects are blocking**

* No need for reactive complexity

4️⃣ **Good enough performance**

* Handles normal traffic easily

---

### 🔹 When WebFlux is used

👉 **Spring WebFlux (less used, but important)**
Used when:

* High **concurrency (many users)**
* **Streaming / real-time apps**
* Need **non-blocking performance**

---

### 🔹 Real Industry Trend

* **~80–90% projects → Spring REST (MVC)**
* **~10–20% → WebFlux (special cases)**

---

### 🔹 One Line

👉 **Spring REST is widely used; WebFlux is used only for high-performance reactive systems**

---

### 🔹 Interview Line

👉 **In most real-world applications, Spring MVC (REST) is commonly used due to its simplicity and wide support, while WebFlux is used in specific scenarios requiring high concurrency and non-blocking behavior.**


but when u send the request to server it is allocationg one thread for one request in Spring MVC (REST) so i guess its makes slow then web flux ? 

You’re thinking in the right direction 👍 but the conclusion needs a small correction.

---

### 🔹 Correct Understanding

👉 Yes, in **Spring MVC (REST)**

* **1 request = 1 thread (blocking model)**

👉 But ❌ **this does NOT automatically mean it is slow**

---

### 🔹 Why it still works fast

1️⃣ **Thread pools are used**

* Server (Tomcat) has **many threads (100–200+)**
  👉 Handles many requests in parallel

---

2️⃣ **Most requests are quick**

* If response is fast (few ms) → thread is free quickly

---

3️⃣ **Hardware scaling**

* More CPU + more instances → more throughput

---

### 🔹 When it becomes slow

👉 Problem happens when:

* Many **slow I/O calls (DB/API)**
* Threads are **waiting (blocked)**
* Thread pool gets **exhausted**

👉 This is where **WebFlux helps** ✅

---

### 🔹 Key Difference

* **Spring MVC**

  * Blocking
  * Good for normal load

* **Spring WebFlux**

  * Non-blocking
  * Better for **high concurrency (1000+ users)**

---

### 🔹 Final Correct Statement

👉 **Spring MVC uses one thread per request, but with proper thread pool and optimization, it performs well. WebFlux is preferred only when handling very high concurrent requests with many blocking I/O operations.**

---

### 🔹 One Line

👉 **Spring MVC is not slow, it just uses more threads; WebFlux uses fewer threads more efficiently**

---

### 🔹 Interview Line

👉 **Although Spring MVC follows a one-thread-per-request model, it performs efficiently with thread pools and scaling; WebFlux is used when we need better resource utilization under high concurrency.**

2. Repository
package com.app.raghu.repo;

import org.springframework.data.mongodb.repository.ReactiveMongoRepository;

import com.app.raghu.entity.Student;

public interface StudentRepository 
  extends ReactiveMongoRepository<Student, String>{

}

3. Service
package com.app.raghu.service;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;

import com.app.raghu.entity.Student;
import com.app.raghu.repo.StudentRepository;

import reactor.core.publisher.Flux;
import reactor.core.publisher.Mono;

@Service
public class StudentService {

  @Autowired
  private StudentRepository repo;

  public Mono<Student> save(Student student) {
    return repo.save(student);
  }

  public Mono<Student> getOne(String id) {
    return repo.findById(id).switchIfEmpty(Mono.empty());
  }

  public Flux<Student> findAll() {
    return repo.findAll().switchIfEmpty(Flux.empty());
  }

  public Mono<Void> delete(String id) {
    return repo.deleteById(id);
  }
}

4. RestController
package com.app.raghu.rest;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PostMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestBody;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

import com.app.raghu.entity.Student;
import com.app.raghu.service.StudentService;

import reactor.core.publisher.Mono;

@RestController
@RequestMapping("/student")
public class StudentRestController {

  @Autowired
  private StudentService service;

  @PostMapping("/create")
  public Mono<Student> save(@RequestBody Student student) {
    return service.save(student);
  }
}

*) PK Field name is taken as _id in Database
*) If we find _class property then it indicates data came from 
  external sources (like Java, .Net ..etc)
*) If we use any other DataType for PK in coding then value will never
  be generated. We need to pass manual value.

5. RestController
package com.app.raghu.rest;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.DeleteMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PathVariable;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PostMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestBody;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RestController;

import com.app.raghu.entity.Student;
import com.app.raghu.service.StudentService;

import reactor.core.publisher.Flux;
import reactor.core.publisher.Mono;

@RestController
@RequestMapping("/student")
public class StudentRestController {

  @Autowired
  private StudentService service;

  @PostMapping("/create")
  public Mono<Student> save(@RequestBody Student student) {
    return service.save(student);
  }
  
  @GetMapping("/fetch/{id}")
  public Mono<Student> getOne(@PathVariable String id) {
    return service.getOne(id);
  }
  
  @GetMapping("/all")
  public Flux<Student> fetchAll() {
    return service.findAll();
  }
  
  @DeleteMapping("/remove/{id}")
  public Mono<Void> deleteOne(@PathVariable String id) {
    return service.delete(id);
    /* service.delete(id);
    return Mono.just("Removed Id "+id); */
  }
  
}

public class TestProducerCallRunner implements CommandLineRunner {

    WebClient client = WebClient.create("http://localhost:9090/student");

        client
        .post() //Http Method
        .uri("/create") //PATH
        .body(Mono.just(new Student("AA256", "SAM", 300.0)), Student.class) //Body
        .retrieve() // execute
        .bodyToMono(Student.class); //convert response
    
    System.out.println("FROM CONSUMER ---->");
    //access result
    result.subscribe(System.out::println);
    */
    
    
    /*
    Flux<Student> flux =  client.get().uri("/all").retrieve().bodyToFlux(Student.class);
    flux.doOnNext(System.out::println).blockLast();
    */
    
    Mono<Student> result = 
    client.get().uri("/fetch/AA256").retrieve() 
    .bodyToMono(Student.class);
    result.subscribe(System.out::println);
  }

}

------------------------------------Lecture-112------------------------------------

  ---------------------------------------------------------------------
            JAAS : Java Authentication and Authorization
               [Security]

*) Authentication : Validating User Login details : username, password
*) Authorization  : Validating User Role to access a service/resources

Ex: BankApplication
  URLs:  /home, /login, /checkBal, /logout, /approveLoan, /openFD ..etc

User:  AJAY/AJAY  Role: Customer
User:  SAM/SAM    Role: Manager
User:  SYED/SYED  Role: Clerk
..etc


Authorization Levels(3):
1. permitAll : A URL/Path can be accessed by every one 
[no login/ no role is required]
Ex: /home, /login, /contactUs, /aboutUs

2. Authenticated: A URL/Path can be accessed only after login
  [any role is valid]

ex: Show Logout Link, First Login , /chagePwd, /logout ..etc

3. hasAuthority: Login must and Valid Role is required

ex: /approveLoan => Login and Role : Manager
    /checkBal    => Login and Role : Customer, Manager

=> Role - String, Authority(I) - SimpleGrantedAuthority(C)
--------------------------------------------------------------
Authentication Type(3):-
1. InMemoryAuthentication 
=> Storing user details inside RAM / Temp Memory.
=> This is only for Testing purpose. (NO database is used)
=> Not Recomanded in production.

2. JDBCAuthentication
=> We use Database to Store user data and roles (1/2 tables)
=> But check details (login details and role details)
   using SQL queries (manually we need to define)
=> less prefered to use in production because : 

### 🔹 Short Answer

👉 **Yes, JDBC Authentication can be used in production, but it is not preferred**

---

### 🔹 Why it is used (rare cases)

1️⃣ **Simple applications**

* Small projects with **basic auth**

2️⃣ **Direct SQL control needed**

* When team wants **full control on queries**

---

### 🔹 Why it is NOT preferred

1️⃣ **Manual SQL queries**

* More code, more maintenance

2️⃣ **Less flexible**

* Hard to customize complex logic

3️⃣ **Not clean (compared to JPA)**

* No object mapping

---

### 🔹 What is preferred instead

👉 **UserDetailsService (JPA / ORM)** ✅

* Clean code
* Flexible
* Industry standard

---

### 🔹 One Line

👉 **JDBC Authentication can be used in production, but ORM-based authentication is preferred**

---

### 🔹 Interview Line

👉 **JDBC Authentication can be used in production for simple use cases, but in real-world applications we prefer UserDetailsService with JPA for better flexibility and maintainability.**


3.*** ORM Authentication/UserDetailsService(Mostly used now a days)
=>means in orm authentication data jpa will handel means data jpa will write query by itself for u u dont need to write manual query by yourself
=> ORM means uses Data JPA, No SQL Query
=> It stores data in Database Table and converts into Object format
   when it is required.
=> Mostly used in production because : 
### 🔹 Mostly Used in Real-Time

👉 **3️⃣ ORM Authentication (UserDetailsService) is mostly used in real projects** ✅

---

### 🔹 Why it is preferred

1️⃣ **Uses JPA / Hibernate**

* No need to write **manual SQL queries**

2️⃣ **Flexible & customizable**

* You can design **your own user table & roles**

3️⃣ **Clean code (Object-oriented)**

* Data handled as **Java objects**

4️⃣ **Production ready**

* Used in almost all **enterprise applications**

---

### 🔹 Other Options

👉 **1️⃣ InMemoryAuthentication**

* Only for **testing / demo** ❌

👉 **2️⃣ JDBCAuthentication**

* Used sometimes
* But **less preferred** (manual SQL, less flexible)

---

### 🔹 One Line

👉 **ORM-based authentication using UserDetailsService is the most commonly used approach in real-time applications**

---

### 🔹 Interview Line

👉 **In real-world applications, we mostly use UserDetailsService with JPA (ORM-based authentication) because it provides flexibility, avoids manual SQL, and is production-ready.**

Dont store plain text password in database 

*) PasswordEncoder:- It is not recomanded to store plain text password
  inside database, better convert into unreadable format ie encoding.

  There is no decode method is given by Spring boot.(because suppose if decode method is there then everyone will decode the password and get the password)
  If we enter Pwd from Login page then that is encoded and compared
  with DB encoded password, if matched then goto Home Page...etc

===coding================================================================
1. We need to define only one class (additionally) for security.
  ie SecurityConfig (any equal name her ename can be anything) called as One Configuration class.

2. This SecurityConfig class contains two methods mainly.
  a. Authentication : InMemory/JDBC/UserDetailsService
  b. Authorization  : permitAll/autnehticated... Login Form + Logout Link


3. ** In Spring Boot 2.6 or before version SecurityConfig class must
   extends one class "WebSecurityConfigurerAdapter".
   but in new Version ie Spring Boot 2.7 or later it is not required.

Old Configuration:
https://github.com/javabyraghu/SpringBoot2SecurityOrmEx/blob/master/src/main/java/in/nareshit/raghu/config/SecurityConfig.java

New Configuration:
https://github.com/javabyraghu/SpringBootSecurityInMemoryEx/blob/main/src/main/java/com/app/raghu/config/WebSecurityConfig.java


return type of authorization is securityfilterchain and return type of authentication is userdetailservice this is in SecurityConfig class. SecurityFilterChain is used for authorization configuration, and UserDetailsService is used for authentication.

In Spring Security, we use SecurityFilterChain to configure authentication and authorization rules, and UserDetailsService is used to load user details for authentication.

*) In our application we need to add one Dependency: Spring Security
in pom.xml
<dependency>
  <groupId>org.springframework.boot</groupId>
  <artifactId>spring-boot-starter-security</artifactId>
</dependency>

Ref Doc:-
https://spring.io/blog/2022/02/21/spring-security-without-the-websecurityconfigureradapter

### 🔹 Your statement (corrected & clear)

👉 **In Spring Security config class:**

* **Authorization → SecurityFilterChain** ✅
* **Authentication → UserDetailsService** ✅

---

### 🔹 Simple Explanation

👉 **SecurityFilterChain (Authorization)**

* Defines **who can access which API**
* Example: `/admin` → only ADMIN

---

👉 **UserDetailsService (Authentication)**

* Loads **user data from DB**
* Used to **verify username & password**

---

### 🔹 Example

```java
@Bean
public SecurityFilterChain securityFilterChain(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
    http.authorizeHttpRequests(auth -> auth
        .requestMatchers("/admin/**").hasRole("ADMIN")
        .anyRequest().authenticated()
    );
    return http.build();
}

@Bean
public UserDetailsService userDetailsService() {
    return username -> {
        // load user from DB
        return new User("user", "password", new ArrayList<>());
    };
}
```

---

### 🔹 One Line

👉 **SecurityFilterChain handles authorization, UserDetailsService handles authentication**

---

### 🔹 Interview Line

👉 **In Spring Security, SecurityFilterChain is used to configure authorization rules, while UserDetailsService is used to load user details for authentication.**

Example code sampels For Authorization:-
1. Accessed by every one : /welcome 

.antMatchers("/welcome").permitAll()

2. Access URL only after Login : /profile

.antMatchers("/profile").authenticated()

3. Access URL after login having role ADMIN : /mydata

.antMatchers("/mydata").hasAuthority("ADMIN")

4. Access URL after login having role MANAGER or CUSTOMER: /checkBal

.antMatchers("/checkBal").hasAnyAuthority("MANAGER", "CUSTOMER")

or 

now in latest version this .antMatchers() is depricated currently we are using .requestmatchers()

like this : 

.requestMatchers("/welcome").permitAll()

.requestMatchers("/profile").authenticated()

.requestMatchers("/mydata").hasAuthority("ADMIN")

.requestMatchers("/checkBal").hasAnyAuthority("MANAGER", "CUSTOMER")

5. To indicates remaining URLs (which are not configured like above)

   .anyRequest().permitAll() // .permitAll() → anyone can access, remaining urls can be accessed by anyone no login is required 
          [or]
   .anyRequest().authenticated() //.authenticated() → login required, All remaining URLs require login (any authenticated user can access)
          [or]
   .anyRequest().hasAuthority("ADMIN") //.hasAuthority("ADMIN") → only ADMIN can access the reaming urls

 you need to write only one not all three .anyRequest() defines access rule for all remaining URLs Use only one .anyRequest() (it is fallback rule)

==============Simple Security Application====================
Name : SpringSecurityInMemoryEx
Dep  : Spring Web, Spring Security, Devtools, Thymeleaf

1. Controller
package com.app.raghu.controller;

import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;

@Controller
public class HomeController {

  @GetMapping({"/home","/"})
  public String showHome() {
    return "home";
  }
  
  @GetMapping("/hello")
  public String showHello() {
    return "hello";
  }
  
  @GetMapping("/login")
  public String showLogin() {
    return "login";
  }
}

2. SecurityConfig
package com.app.raghu.config;

import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.builders.HttpSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configuration.EnableWebSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.core.userdetails.User;
import org.springframework.security.core.userdetails.UserDetails;
import org.springframework.security.core.userdetails.UserDetailsService;
import org.springframework.security.provisioning.InMemoryUserDetailsManager;
import org.springframework.security.web.SecurityFilterChain;

@Configuration
@EnableWebSecurity
public class SecurityConfig {

  // 2. Authorization
  @Bean
  public SecurityFilterChain configurePaths(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
    http.authorizeHttpRequests(
        request -> request.antMatchers("/","/home").permitAll()
        .anyRequest().authenticated()
        )
      .formLogin( form -> form.loginPage("/login").permitAll() )
      .logout( logout -> logout.permitAll() );
      
    return http.build();
  }
  
  //old style
  /*
  public void configure(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
    http.authorizeRequests()
    .antMatchers("/","/home").permitAll()
    .anyRequest().authenticated()
    
    .and()
    .formLogin()
    .loginPage("/login")
    .defaultSuccessUrl("/hello")
    
    .and()
    .logout()
    .logoutRequestMatcher(new AntPathRequestMatcher("/logout"))
    .logoutSuccessUrl("/login?logout");
  }
  */
  
  

  // 1. Authentication (InMemory)
  @Bean
  public UserDetailsService userDetailsService() {

    UserDetails user = User.withDefaultPasswordEncoder()
        .username("sam").password("sam").roles("ADMIN")
        .build();
    
    UserDetails user2 = User.withDefaultPasswordEncoder()
        .username("ram").password("ram").roles("CUSTOMER")
        .build();
    
    return new InMemoryUserDetailsManager(user,user2);
  }

}

        <title>Spring Security Example </title>
    </head>
    <body>
        <div th:if="${param.error}">
            Invalid username and password.
        </div>
        <div th:if="${param.logout}">
            You have been logged out.
        </div>
        <br/>
        <form th:action="@{/login}" method="post">
            <div><label> User Name : <input type="text" name="username"/> </label></div>
            <div><label> Password: <input type="password" name="password"/> </label></div>
            <div><input type="submit" value="Sign In"/></div>
        </form>
    </body>
</html>

       Spring Boot Security - using JDBC

*) InMemoryAuthentication : Recomanded to use in Dev Environment only.
  It is for testing purpose. Do not use in Production.

*) To store/fetch user details using Database, we use JDBC API.
*) Here we are going to use PasswordEncoder to add user data.

Two tables are created to store user data
  users (username, password, enabled)
  authorities(username, authority)


*) Password encoder is recomanded to use to encode and store passwords
  in database tables.

    BCryptPasswordEncoder encoder = new BCryptPasswordEncoder();

Database Setup:
create table users(
  username varchar(50) not null primary key,
  password varchar(500) not null,
  enabled boolean not null);

create table authorities (
  username varchar(50) not null,
  authority varchar(50) not null,
  constraint fk_authorities_users foreign key(username) 
  references users(username));

create unique index ix_auth_username on authorities (username,authority);

package com.app.raghu.controller;

import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;

@Controller
public class HomeController {

  //EVERY ONCE CAN ACCESS
  // .antMatchers("/home").permitAll
  @GetMapping({"/home","/"})
  public String showHome() {
    return "home";
  }
  
  //ONLY AFTER LOGIN
  // .antMatchers("/hello").authenticated()
  @GetMapping("/hello")
  public String showHello() {
    return "hello";
  }
  
  //ONLY ADMIN After login
  // .antMatchers("/admin").hasAuthority("ADMIN")
  @GetMapping("/admin")
  public String showAdmin() {
    return "admin";
  }
  
  //ONLY CUSTOMER After login
  // .antMatchers("/customer").hasAuthority("CUSTOMER")
  @GetMapping("/customer")
  public String showCustomer() {
    return "customer";
  }
  
  @GetMapping("/login")
  public String showLogin() {
    return "login";
  }
}

2. Security Config
package com.app.raghu.config;

import javax.sql.DataSource;

import org.springframework.context.annotation.Bean;
import org.springframework.context.annotation.Configuration;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.builders.HttpSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.config.annotation.web.configuration.EnableWebSecurity;
import org.springframework.security.core.userdetails.User;
import org.springframework.security.core.userdetails.UserDetails;
import org.springframework.security.core.userdetails.UserDetailsService;
import org.springframework.security.crypto.bcrypt.BCryptPasswordEncoder;
import org.springframework.security.provisioning.JdbcUserDetailsManager;
import org.springframework.security.web.SecurityFilterChain;

@Configuration
@EnableWebSecurity
public class SecurityConfig {
  
  @Bean
  public BCryptPasswordEncoder passwordEncoder() {
    return new BCryptPasswordEncoder();
  }

  //authorization
  @Bean
  public SecurityFilterChain configureAuth(HttpSecurity http) throws Exception {
    http.authorizeHttpRequests(
        request->request.antMatchers("/home","/").permitAll()
            .antMatchers("/admin").hasAuthority("ADMIN")
            .antMatchers("/customer").hasAuthority("CUSTOMER")
            .anyRequest().authenticated()
        )
    .formLogin(
        form->form.loginPage("/login").permitAll()
        .defaultSuccessUrl("/hello", true)
        )
    .logout(logout->logout.permitAll()) ;
    
    
    return http.build();
  }
  
  //authentication
  @Bean
  public UserDetailsService userDetailsService(DataSource datasource) {
    UserDetails user1  = User.withUsername("sam")
        .password("$2a$10$TD7ldmKUQw3EHFxVivyA8OUrzy7butY9QDRnltnBS/b9aI0j6reYq")
        .authorities("ADMIN").build();
    
    UserDetails user2  = User.withUsername("ram")
        .password("$2a$10$dEm8gdOC0R2S7IgXSnBKFOSeeKbCNuVeMC/hP24eY7zdADlUif4n.")
        .authorities("CUSTOMER").build();
    
    JdbcUserDetailsManager users = new JdbcUserDetailsManager(datasource);
    users.createUser(user1);
    users.createUser(user2);
    
    return users;
  }


}

S#4 Entity class
package com.app.raghu.entity;

import java.util.Set;

import javax.persistence.CollectionTable;
import javax.persistence.Column;
import javax.persistence.ElementCollection;
import javax.persistence.Entity;
import javax.persistence.GeneratedValue;
import javax.persistence.GenerationType;
import javax.persistence.Id;
import javax.persistence.JoinColumn;
import javax.persistence.Table;

import lombok.AllArgsConstructor;
import lombok.Data;
import lombok.NoArgsConstructor;

//so here two tables are created in one entity class
@Data
@NoArgsConstructor
@AllArgsConstructor
@Entity
@Table(name="usertab") //this is the user table main table
public class User {
  @Id
  @GeneratedValue(strategy = GenerationType.IDENTITY)
  @Column(name="uid")
  private Integer userId;
  
  @Column(name="uname")
  private String userName;
  
  @Column(name="umail")
  private String userEmail;
  
  @Column(name="upwd")
  private String userPwd;
  
  //why it is collection because user can have many roles a user can be admin for his //work and this user can be a customer to book his own tickets 
  // One user → multiple roles → so we use collection
  //We use @ElementCollection because a single user can have multiple roles, so roles //are stored as a collection (Set) in a separate table. 
  @ElementCollection
  @CollectionTable(name="roles_tab", ////this is 2nd table role table
    joinColumns = @JoinColumn(name="uid")
  )
  @Column(name="urole")
  private Set<String> userRoles;
  
}

@ElementCollection

Used to store multiple simple values (like String roles) for one entity
Example: one user → many roles

👉 @CollectionTable

Defines the separate table where those values are stored
Also defines foreign key (join with main table)

S#6 Service interface/class
package com.app.raghu.service;

import java.util.Optional;

import com.app.raghu.entity.User;

public interface IUserService {

  Integer saveUser(User user);
  Optional<User> getOneUser(Integer id);
}
--------------
package com.app.raghu.service.impl;

import java.util.Optional;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Service;

import com.app.raghu.entity.User;
import com.app.raghu.repo.UserRepository;
import com.app.raghu.service.IUserService;

@Service
public class UserServiceImpl implements IUserService {

  @Autowired
  private UserRepository repo;
  
  public Integer saveUser(User user) {
    return repo.save(user).getUserId();
  }

  public Optional<User> getOneUser(Integer id) {
    return repo.findById(id);
  }

}


7. Controller
package com.app.raghu.controller;

import org.springframework.beans.factory.annotation.Autowired;
import org.springframework.stereotype.Controller;
import org.springframework.ui.Model;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.GetMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.ModelAttribute;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.PostMapping;
import org.springframework.web.bind.annotation.RequestMapping;

import com.app.raghu.entity.User;
import com.app.raghu.service.IUserService;

@Controller
@RequestMapping("/user")
public class UserController {

  @Autowired
  private IUserService service;
  
  //1. show Register page
  @GetMapping("/register")
  public String showReg() {
    return "UserRegister";
  }
  
  //2. save user data
  @PostMapping("/save")
  public String saveUser(
      @ModelAttribute User user, Model model)
  {
    Integer id = service.saveUser(user);
    String message = "User '"+id+"' created!";
    model.addAttribute("message", message);
    return "UserRegister";
  }
  
  
}

    Custom UserDetailsService (ORM)

ok iam giving it a clear flow how internally it works : 
first we go to login page here we enter userrname and password then it goes to SecurityConfig file and here SecurityConfig  goes to database via UserDetailService interface which is having loadUserByUsername method and then it goes to database and load this data into entity object because entity class holds the data of the user which u entered in login  so entity fetched the data and with the help of username and now then Entity data is converted into Spring Security User object(it is also a kind of entity class but this is spring security user entity class) so that Spring Security can perform authentication and authorization then it goes to DaoAuthenticationProvider (which checks password is correct or not) if not correct then it goes  to again login page and if it is correct then login success full and it will show u logout button as well and if u press logout it goes to login page again 
this is how it actually works
